###begin article-title 0
###xml 53 77 53 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 53 77 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
Elevated dNTP levels suppress hyper-recombination in Saccharomyces cerevisiae S-phase checkpoint mutants
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 196 203 196 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 222 227 222 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad52</italic>
###xml 507 514 507 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 710 714 710 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 794 801 794 801 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 918 922 918 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 1079 1086 1079 1086 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 1088 1092 1088 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 1097 1109 1097 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 1136 1167 1136 1167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1, mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic>
###xml 1172 1176 1172 1176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 1255 1272 1243 1260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic>
###xml 1360 1372 1336 1348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 20 25 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 41 46 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
MEC1, the essential yeast homolog of the human ATR/ATM genes, controls the S-phase checkpoint and prevents replication fork collapse at slow zones of DNA replication. The viability of hypomorphic mec1-21 is reduced in the rad52 mutant, defective in homologous recombination, suggesting that replication generates recombinogenic lesions. We previously observed a 6-, 10- and 30-fold higher rate of spontaneous sister chromatid exchange (SCE), heteroallelic recombination and translocations, respectively, in mec1-21 mutants compared to wild-type. Here we report that the hyper-recombination phenotype correlates with lower deoxyribonucleoside triphosphate (dNTP) levels, compared to wild-type. By introducing a dun1 mutation, thus eliminating inducible expression of ribonucleotide reductase in mec1-21, rates of spontaneous SCE increased 15-fold above wild-type. All the hyper-recombination phenotypes were reduced by SML1 deletions, which increase dNTP levels. Measurements of dNTP pools indicated that, compared to wild-type, there was a significant decrease in dNTP levels in mec1-21, dun1 and mec1-21 dun1, while the dNTP levels of mec1-21 sml1, mec1-21 dun1 sml1 and sml1 mutants were approximately2-fold higher. Interestingly, higher dNTP levels in mec1-21 dun1 sml1 correlate with approximately2-fold higher rate of spontaneous mutagenesis, compared to mec1-21 dun1. We suggest that higher dNTP levels in specific checkpoint mutants suppress the formation of recombinogenic lesions.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
INTRODUCTION
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 37 38 37 38 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 175 179 175 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rad3</italic>
###xml 190 194 190 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 328 332 328 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 360 364 360 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 409 419 409 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1, CRT1</italic>
###xml 423 428 423 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DIF1,</italic>
###xml 454 458 454 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNR1</italic>
###xml 462 466 462 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNR3</italic>
###xml 548 552 548 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 711 715 711 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 727 728 727 728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 22 27 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 47 52 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
MEC1 is the essential yeast homolog (1) of the human ATR/ATM genes (for review, 2) and shares some functions with both ATM (mutated in ataxia telangiectasia) and ATR (ATM and Rad3 related). MEC1 prevents replication fork collapse (3), a function shared with ATR, but not ATM, in mammalian cells (for review, 2). Similar to ATR, MEC1 is required for viability; mec1 lethality can be suppressed by mutations in SML1, CRT1 or DIF1, or by over-expression of RNR1 or RNR3, all of which increase the activity of ribonucleotide reductase (for review, 4). SML1 mutations elevate deoxyribonucleoside triphosphate (dNTP) levels 2-fold compared to wild-type, implying that increasing dNTP levels is sufficient to suppress mec1 lethality (5).
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 58 63 58 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD53</italic>
###xml 131 135 131 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 184 185 184 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 199 203 199 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 208 213 208 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD53</italic>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 252 253 252 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 296 300 296 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 305 310 305 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad53</italic>
###xml 355 356 355 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 462 466 462 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sml1</italic>
###xml 516 520 516 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 522 523 522 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 532 537 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
MEC1's function in controlling dNTP levels is mediated by RAD53, which, upon activation by DNA damage and in S phase, triggers the DUN1-mediated induction of ribonucleotide reductase (6). While both MEC1 and RAD53 are essential, DUN1 is non-essential (7). Basal dNTP levels are lower in specific mec1 and rad53 hypomorphic mutants, compared to wild-type (8). Observations that dun1 exhibits a longer S phase than wild-type and is defective in the degradation of Sml1 suggest that basal dNTP levels are also lower in dun1 (9). Thus, yeast can maintain viability at dNTP levels that are both higher and lower than in wild-type.
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 261 265 261 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 340 342 340 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 427 429 427 429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 451 455 451 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNR1</italic>
###xml 537 538 537 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 576 578 576 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 585 594 585 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnr1-D57N</italic>
###xml 705 707 705 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 864 866 864 866 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
Lower dNTP levels may correlate with a hyper-recombination phenotype and decreased spontaneous point mutation rates while higher dNTP levels may correlate with an increase in spontaneous or DNA damage-associated mutagenesis, compared to wild-type. For example, dun1 mutants exhibit higher levels of spontaneous heteroallelic recombination (10) and lower levels of spontaneous mutagenesis that results in canavanine resistance (11). Over-expression of RNR1, which results in higher dNTP levels, leads to higher levels of 4-nitroquinoline-N-oxide (4NQO)-associated mutagenesis (12). The rnr1-D57N mutant, which has 2- to 3-fold higher dNTP levels, exhibits a similar increase in spontaneous mutation rates (13). One possible explanation is that replicative DNA polymerases may require higher levels of dNTPs for insertion of particular bases opposite damaged sites (12).
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 6 10 6 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 32 36 32 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 224 231 224 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 279 280 279 280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 281 283 281 283 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 379 381 379 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 384 389 384 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD52</italic>
###xml 467 475 467 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21,</italic>
###xml 493 506 493 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 rad52</italic>
###xml 600 607 600 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 609 611 609 611 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 678 685 678 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 830 832 830 832 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 885 890 885 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD52</italic>
###xml 916 918 916 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
Since mec1 null mutants require sml1 for viability, mec1 hypomorphic mutants that retain essential function are useful in determining which genetic instability phenotypes correlate to lower dNTP levels. Such mutants include mec1-21, which is defective in the S-phase checkpoint (6,14) and results from a G to A substitution (G882S) at position 2644 outside of the kinase domain (15). RAD52 is required for double-strand break repair (for review, 16), and compared to mec1-21, viability in the mec1-21 rad52 mutant is significantly reduced, suggesting that double-strand breaks spontaneously arise in mec1-21 (17). Our previous studies have indicated that compared to wild-type, mec1-21 exhibits significantly higher rates of spontaneous homologous recombination between sister chromatids, homologs and non-homologous chromosomes (18). The hyper-recombination phenotype is dependent on RAD52 and G2 checkpoint genes (18), suggesting that spontaneous DNA breaks generated by DNA replication are repaired by homologous recombination.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 44 51 44 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 85 89 85 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 158 162 158 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 166 178 166 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 350 354 350 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
We demonstrate that, compared to wild-type, mec1-21 hyper-recombination phenotype is SML1-dependent and correlates with lower basal levels of dNTPs. Deleting SML1 in mec1-21 dun1 mutant also correlates to a modestly higher rate of spontaneous mutagenesis. These studies suggest that higher dNTP levels may suppress hyper-recombination in hypomorphic mec1 mutants. Thus, an adequate supply of dNTPs is an important MEC1 function in maintaining genomic stability.
###end p 7
###begin title 8
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 8
###begin title 9
###xml 10 15 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Media and yeast strains
###end title 9
###begin p 10
###xml 242 248 242 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 250 252 250 252 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 34 39 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 171 176 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Standard media for the culture of yeast, SC (synthetic complete, dextrose), SC-HIS (SC lacking histidine), SC-TRP (SC lacking tryptophan), SC-URA (SC lacking uracil), YP (yeast extract, peptone) and YPD (YP, dextrose), are described by Burke et al. (19). YP(A)D contains YPD with 80 mg/l adenine. CAN plates contain SC medium and 60 mg/l of canavanine.
###end p 10

###xml 9 14 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 916 921 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Relevant yeast strains are listed in Table 1. The mec1-21 strain YA197 (Y620), and the YA184 and YA185 strains used to PCR amplify sml1::URA3 and mec1-Delta::TRP1, respectively, are derived from W303; all other strains are of the S288c background. Strains used to measure SCE contain two overlapping his3 fragments, positioned in tandem at trp1, and were derived from YB163 (20,21). Diploid strains were used to measure translocations that were derived from a cross of one haploid (YB109) that contains the his3 fragments on one copy of chromosomes II and IV, and another which did not contain the his3 fragments (YA102) (22). To measure heteroallelic recombination, we replaced the ade2-101 alleles in YB109 and YA102 with ade2-n (YB318) and ade2-a (YB315), respectively, by two-step gene replacement using the plasmid pKH9 (23). Heteroallelic recombination was measured by selecting for Ade+ recombinants. ###begin p 14
###xml 12 19 12 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 87 90 87 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 90 91 90 91 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</bold>
###xml 91 98 91 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 114 115 114 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 194 196 194 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 296 300 296 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">his3</italic>
###xml 362 373 362 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1::KanMX</italic>
###xml 378 388 378 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1::URA3</italic>
###xml 479 490 479 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1::KanMX</italic>
###xml 494 504 494 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1::URA3</italic>
###xml 627 649 627 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec-&#916;1 sml1::KanMX</italic>
###xml 681 683 677 679 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 399 404 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
We used the mec1-21 missense mutant to measure spontaneous recombination. The original MATamec1-21 strain (Y620) (6) was backcrossed 10 times with strains in the S288c background [YB163, YA166 (21) and YB315] to generate meiotic segregants that either do (YB312) or do not (YB316, YB314) contain his3 recombinational substrates to measure SCE. We introduced the sml1::KanMX and sml1::URA3 allele in yeast strains by PCR-mediated gene replacement; the primers used for amplifying sml1::KanMX or sml1::URA3 knockout fragments were the same: 5'-CATATCGTTACTGTTTTGGAACATCGC-3' and 5'-TAAAGGGAAAGGAAAATGCACG-3'. The construction of mec-Delta1 sml1::KanMX (YB327) was described earlier (17).
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 61 65 61 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 178 180 178 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 208 212 208 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">his3</italic>
###xml 242 248 242 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ade2-n</italic>
###xml 290 296 290 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ade2-a</italic>
###xml 375 378 375 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 378 379 378 379 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</bold>
###xml 379 398 379 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-inc ade2-n mec1-21</italic>
###xml 443 461 443 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAL1::his3-&#916;5&#8242;</italic>
###xml 466 484 462 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trp1::his3-&#916;3&#8242;</italic>
###xml 508 515 500 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
To measure translocations and heteroallelic recombination in mec1 strains, mutations were introduced into two haploids by either genetic crosses or by one-step gene replacement (24); one haploid contains the his3 recombination substrates and ade2-n (YB318), while another (YB315) contained ade2-a but no recombination substrates. YB318 was crossed with YB313 to generate the MATa-inc ade2-n mec1-21 meiotic segregant (YB319) that contains the GAL1::his3-Delta5' and trp1::his3-Delta3'. YB325 is a homozygous mec1-21 diploid that was then used to measure translocations and heteroallelic recombination.
###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 76 78 76 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 201 212 201 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1::KanMX</italic>
###xml 290 291 290 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8242;</italic>
###xml 290 291 290 291 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>&#8242;</italic></bold>
###xml 319 349 319 349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1::KanMX sml1::URA3</italic>
###xml 381 391 381 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1::URA3</italic>
###xml 397 416 397 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1::KanMX</italic>
###xml 454 456 454 456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
Additional checkpoint mutants were made by either one-step gene disruption (24) or by genetic crosses and screening the phenotype of the appropriate meiotic segregant. The primer pairs used to amplify dun1::KanMX fragments were, 5'AGAAGCCCCTGAATACCATAAATA3' and 5'CGATGTCAGAGATTTAGAGGAAAAA3', respectively. We made the mec1-21 dun1::KanMX sml1::URA3 haploid (YB380) by introducing sml1::URA3 into mec1-21 dun1::KanMX (YB369) by one-step gene disruption (24). All gene disruptions were confirmed by PCR.
###end p 16
###begin title 17
Determining rates of spontaneous recombination and mutations
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 118 122 118 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAN1</italic>
###xml 168 170 168 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 198 200 198 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 344 345 344 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 382 386 382 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAN1</italic>
###xml 517 519 517 519 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
The rates (events per cell division) of spontaneous SCE, heteroallelic recombination, translocations and mutations in CAN1 were determined by the method of the median (25), as previously performed (21). Rates of spontaneous heteroallelic recombination were determined on cells inoculated on YP(A)D, on which there is no growth advantage for Ade+ recombinants. Rates of mutations in CAN1 were determined by selecting for resistance to canavanine. We determined the statistical significance by the Mann-Whitney U-test (26).
###end p 18
###begin title 19
Determining dNTP levels
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 67 73 67 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 76 78 76 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 110 111 110 111 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 124 125 124 125 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 155 156 143 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">8</sup>
###xml 396 397 376 377 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 645 646 619 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 977 978 947 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 1221 1222 1179 1180 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 1225 1226 1183 1184 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 34 39 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The methods of measuring dNTPs in yeast are as described in Chabes et al., (13). At a density between 0.5 x 107 and 1.5 x 107 cells/ml, approximately1 x 108 cells were harvested by filtration through 25 mm White AAWP nitrocellulose filters (0.8 microm, Millipore AB, Solna, Sweden). The filters were immersed in 500 microl of ice-cold extraction solution (12% w/v trichloroacetic acid, 15 mM MgCl2) in Eppendorf tubes. The following steps were carried out at 4degreesC. The tubes were vortexed for 30 s, incubated for 15 min and vortexed again for 30 s. The filters were removed and the supernatants were collected after centrifugation at 20 000g for 1 min and added to 800 microl of ice-cold Freon-trioctylamine mixture [10 ml of Freon (1,1,2-trichlorotrifluoroethane, Aldrich, Sigma-Aldrich Sweden AB, Stockholm, Sweden, 99%) and 2.8 ml of trioctylamine (Fluka, Sigma-Aldrich Sweden AB, Stockholm, Sweden, >99%)]. The samples were vortexed and centrifuged for 1 min at 20 000g. The aqueous phase was collected and added to 800 microl of ice-cold Freon-trioctylamine mixture. The mixture was vortexed and centrifuged as described earlier. A 475 microl aliquot of the aqueous phase was pH-adjusted with 25 microl of 1M NH4HCO3, pH 8.9, the deoxyribonucleotides were separated from the ribonucleotides by boronate affinity chromatography (Affi-Gel 601, Bio-Rad) and quantified by HPLC. Another 47.5 microl aliquot of the aqueous phase was mixed with 152.5 microl of water and used for the HPLC quantification of NTP pools. Separation of nucleotides was done on a Partisphere 5 SAX column (PolyLC Inc., Columbia, MD, USA) using a UV-2075 Plus detector (Jasco, Molndal, Sweden). Nucleotides were isocratically eluted with 2.5% acetonitrile, 0.36 M ammonium phosphate, pH 3.4 buffer.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
Western blots
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 112 115 112 115 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 229 232 225 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bis</italic>
###xml 391 395 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
###xml 401 406 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To detect Rad53 phosphorylation after HU and MMS exposure, protein samples were obtained from log phase cells (A600 = 0.5-1) exposed to 200 mM HU or 0.01% MMS for 2 h. Proteins (10 microg) were separated on 10% acrylamide/0.266% bis-acrylamide gels, transferred to nitrocellulose membrane and exposed to a Rad53 antibody (yC-19, Santa Cruz). The secondary antibody was peroxidase conjugated goat anti-mouse IgG (Jackson ImmunoResearch Laboratory, Inc.). The signals were developed using ECL western lightning kit (NEL102, PerkinElmer Life Science, Inc.).
###end p 22

(<bold>B</bold>) Translocation events result from recombination between the same <italic>his3</italic> fragments located each on chromosomes II and IV. Positions of the <italic>GAL1</italic> and <italic>trp1</italic> are shown on chromosomes II, IV and the reciprocal translocation. (<bold>C</bold>) Heteroallelic recombination between <italic>ade2-a</italic> and <italic>ade2-n</italic> generates <italic>ADE2. ADE2</italic> and <italic>ade2</italic> alleles are represented as boxes; <italic>ade2-a</italic> and <italic>ade2-n</italic> are separated by &#8764;1 kb.</p>

Viability of particular mec1 hypomorphs is reduced in the rad52 mutant, deficient in homologous recombination (27,17). While approximately60% of either mec1-21 or rad52 log phase cells form colonies, only approximately20% of mec1-21 rad52 cells form colonies (17). Deleting SML1 in mec1-21 rad52 increased the plating efficiency to approximately50% and increased the growth rate to wild-type levels (). These results suggest that deleting SML1 in mec1-21 rad52 decreases the number of lethal DNA double-strand breaks. We therefore determined whether hyper-recombination phenotypes of mec1-21 would be suppressed by SML1 deletions and correlate with dNTP levels. Unequal SCE was measured by selecting for His+ recombinants in haploid strains containing two truncated his3 gene fragments (20,21, Figure 1). Diploid strains were used to measure heteroallelic recombination between ade2-a and ade2-n (28) and ectopic recombination between GAL1::his3-Delta5' and trp1::his3-Delta3' (22, Figure 1). Figure 1.Unequal SCE, translocation and heteroallelic recombination assays used in this study. Ovals represent centromeres and lines represent chromosomes. For simplicity, the left arms of chromosomes are not included. An arrow and feathers together denote HIS3. As indicated in the bottom left of the figure, the 5' deletion lacks the feather and the 3' deletion lacks the arrow. The two regions of the sequence identity shared by the his3 fragments are indicated by decorated boxes; closely-spaced diagonal-filled boxes indicate a region of 167 bp and the broadly-spaced diagonal line-filled boxes indicate a region of approximately300bp. The 117-bp HO cut site (HOcs), as indicated by an arrowhead, is located between these sequences within the his3-Delta3'::HOcs fragment. (A) The his3-truncated fragments are integrated into the trp1 locus to measure unequal SCE events. (B) Translocation events result from recombination between the same his3 fragments located each on chromosomes II and IV. Positions of the GAL1 and trp1 are shown on chromosomes II, IV and the reciprocal translocation. (C) Heteroallelic recombination between ade2-a and ade2-n generates ADE2. ADE2 and ade2 alleles are represented as boxes; ade2-a and ade2-n are separated by approximately1 kb.
###end p 24

0.7</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">2.8</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB327</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>mec1-&#916;sml1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.2 &#177; 0.2</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.2</td></tr></tbody></table><table-wrap-foot><fn id="TF2"><p textid="29"><sup>a</sup>All strains derived from S288c. For complete genotype (<xref ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>).</p></fn><fn id="TF3"><p textid="30"><sup>b</sup>Rate represents the number of events per cell division; <italic>n</italic> &#8805; 3.</p></fn><fn id="TF4"><p textid="31"><sup>c</sup>Ratio represents rate of SCE in mutant/rate of SCE in wild&#8211;type.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
We reasoned that if lower dNTP levels correlate with higher recombination rates in mec1 mutants, then SML1 mutations would decrease homologous recombination in mec1-21 mutants. We previously observed a 6-fold increase in the rate of spontaneous SCE in the mec1-21 mutant (YB312) compared to wild-type (18). We observed no difference in the rates of spontaneous recombination between sml1 (YB326) and wild-type (YB163); however the 6-fold increase in rates of SCE was reduced to wild-type levels in mec1-21 sml1 (YB329, Table 2). For complete genotype (Table 1).bRate represents the number of events per cell division; n >/= 3.cRatio represents rate of SCE in mutant/rate of SCE in wild-type.

###xml 1166 1623 1148 1605 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F2" position="float"><label>Figure 2.</label><caption><p textid="37">Heteroallelic recombination in <italic>mec1-21</italic> and <italic>mec1-21 sml1</italic> is exhibited by a colony sector assay in diploid strains. <italic>ADE2</italic> results from heteroallelic recombination between <italic>ade2-a</italic> and <italic>ade2-n</italic> generates; red sectors are Ade<sup>&#8722;</sup> and white sectors are Ade<sup>+</sup>(<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>). Rates of heteroallelic recombination and translocations in mec1-21 were 10-fold higher and 23-fold higher than wild-type, respectively (Table 3). We determined whether mec1-21 hyper-recombination between homologs and non-homologs also required SML1. Heteroallelic recombination between ade2 alleles can be visualized using a colony pigment assay, where Ade+ recombinants appear as white colony sectors (Figure 2). Heavily white sectored colonies indicated that more heteroallelic recombination occurred in mec1-21 (YB325) than in wild-type (YB348), while the mec1-21 sml1 mutant (YB375) exhibited less visible sectoring than mec1-21 cells (Figure 2). ###xml 243 244 243 244 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 282 286 282 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>

###begin p 38
###xml 175 176 175 176 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 257 261 257 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 306 313 306 313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 316 328 316 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 465 472 465 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 512 524 512 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 599 606 599 606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 615 619 615 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 632 639 632 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
We then measured rates of translocations and heteroallelic recombination in cells grown on medium containing excess adenine (YPAD) so that there is no growth advantage for Ade+ cells. While the rates of heteroallelic recombination and translocations in the sml1 (YB323) and wild-type (YB348) were similar (Table 3), mec1-21 sml1 diploid mutant (YB375) exhibited 8- and 4-fold lower rates of heteroallelic recombination and translocations, respectively, compared to mec1-21. However the rates of recombination in mec1-21 sml1 were still between 2- and 5-fold higher than those observed in wild-type (Table 3). Thus, SML1 deletion in mec1-21 diploid partially suppresses spontaneous heteroallelic recombination and translocations.
###end p 38
###begin title 39
###xml 27 34 27 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 60 64 60 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
Rate of spontaneous SCE in mec1-21 are further increased by dun1
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 120 121 120 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 122 123 122 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 124 126 124 126 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 211 218 211 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 355 362 343 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 396 406 384 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 442 443 426 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 499 506 483 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 606 608 590 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
The MEC1-mediated pathway for regulating dNTP levels involves Rad53 activation, which in turn leads to Dun1 activation (7,9,29). By western blots, we observed that Rad53 is partially activated to P-Rad53 in the mec1-21 hypomorph, compared to wild-type, after HU and MMS exposure (). We observed approximately40% of the Rad53 activation (P-Rad53/Rad53) in mec1-21, compared to wild-type, while in mec1-Delta, the level of activation was <30% (n = 2). These data are consistent with observations that mec1-21 exhibits partial checkpoint activation after exposure to agents that cause DNA replication stress (30).
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 17 21 17 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 71 74 71 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNR</italic>
###xml 82 83 82 83 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 133 134 133 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 154 166 154 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 245 252 245 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 322 326 322 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 407 419 407 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 458 465 458 465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 468 472 468 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 529 541 529 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 621 625 621 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 654 661 654 661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 669 673 669 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 750 762 750 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
Considering that DUN1 is required for transcriptional induction of the RNR genes (7) and is suggested to maintain basal dNTP levels (9), we asked whether mec1-21 dun1 mutants would exhibit higher levels of spontaneous recombination, compared to mec1-21. Although there is no difference between spontaneous rates of SCE in dun1 (YB370) and wild-type, we observed a 15-fold increase in the rate of SCE in the mec1-21 dun1 double mutant, compared to wild-type (Table 2). SML1 mutations conferred significantly lower rates of SCE in mec1-21 dun1 (YB369), but were still 3-fold higher than wild-type. These data indicate that DUN1 suppresses recombination in mec1-21, but a SML1 deletion only partially suppresses the hyper-recombination phenotype of the mec1-21 dun1 double mutant.
###end p 41
###begin title 42
###xml 18 31 18 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21, dun1</italic>
###xml 36 48 36 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 70 82 70 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 87 104 87 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic>
dNTP are lower in mec1-21, dun1 and mec1-21 dun1 but are increased in mec1-21 sml1 and mec1-21 dun1 sml1 mutants compared to wild-type
###end title 42

###xml 1160 1167 1132 1139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 936 1169 912 1141 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="44">dNTP levels measured in wild-type (YB163), <italic>dun1</italic> (YB370), <italic>sml1 </italic>(YB326), <italic>mec1-21 dun1</italic> (YB369), <italic>mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic> (YB380) and <italic>mec1-21</italic> (YB312 and YB311) mutants. ###xml 1169 1169 1141 1141 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp1064f3"/>
###xml 927 1169 903 1141 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F3" position="float"><label>Figure 3.</label><caption><p textid="44">dNTP levels measured in wild-type (YB163), <italic>dun1</italic> (YB370), <italic>sml1 </italic>(YB326), <italic>mec1-21 dun1</italic> (YB369), <italic>mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic> (YB380) and <italic>mec1-21</italic> (YB312 and YB311) mutants. Two <italic>mec1-21</italic> strains were used; YB311 <italic>MAT</italic><bold>a</bold><italic>-inc</italic> and YB312 <italic>MAT&#945;</italic> (<xref ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>).</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp1064f3"/></fig>
###xml 813 818 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
We expected that the higher and lower rates of homologous recombination exhibited by S-phase checkpoint mutants would inversely correlate with dNTP levels. We measured dNTP levels in wild-type, sml1, mec1-21, dun1, mec1-21 sml1, mec1-21 dun1 and mec1-21 dun1 sml1 strains (Figure 3). In comparison to wild-type, the S288c sml1 strains exhibited increased dNTP levels over 100%, while the S288c dun1 strains exhibited approximately50-70% reduction in dNTP levels. The mec1-21 levels of dNTPs were approximately50-70% of those observed in wild-type strains. Interestingly, the dNTP levels of mec1-21 dun1 strains were similar to mec1-21. These results are consistent with observations that MEC1 is epistatic to DUN1 in controlling dNTP levels (6,8). We do not know the lowest dNTP level that maintains viability in yeast; thus, it is possible that basal dNTP levels cannot be reduced further than those observed in mec1-21 dun1. Figure 3.dNTP levels measured in wild-type (YB163), dun1 (YB370), sml1 (YB326), mec1-21 dun1 (YB369), mec1-21 dun1 sml1 (YB380) and mec1-21 (YB312 and YB311) mutants. Two mec1-21 strains were used; YB311 MATa-inc and YB312 MATalpha (Table 1).
###end p 43

###begin p 45
###xml 38 42 38 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 44 56 44 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 61 78 61 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mecl-21 dun1 sml1</italic>
###xml 138 146 126 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 225 237 213 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 246 263 234 251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic>
###xml 285 292 273 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 297 308 285 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21dun1</italic>
###xml 358 366 346 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 403 407 391 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 531 535 519 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 540 544 528 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 589 590 577 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 591 592 579 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 678 685 666 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
The basal dNTP levels were similar in sml1, mec1-21 sml1 and mecl-21 dun1 sml1, and increased approximately2-fold, relative to wild-type (Figure 3). The basal level of each dNTP was elevated between 2- and 4-fold in both the mec1-21 sml1 and the mec1-21 dun1 sml1 strains, relative to mec1-21 and mec1-21dun1, which exhibit lower dNTP levels than wild-type (Figure 3). These data indicate that deleting SML1 in both checkpoint mutants and wild-type leads to similar dNTP levels. These results are consistent with observations that MEC1 and DUN1 both function in a pathway to degrade Sml1 (8,9). Thus, higher dNTP levels correlate with suppression of homologous recombination in mec1-21 mutants.
###end p 45

Spontaneous mutagenesis rates are lower in the mec1-21 dun1 mutant but increased in mec1-21 dun1 sml1 mutants

###xml 913 1400 901 1372 <table-wrap xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="T4" position="float"><label>Table 4.</label><caption><p textid="48">Rates of spontaneous canavanine resistance in <italic>mec1</italic> mutants</p></caption><table frame="hsides" rules="groups"><thead align="left"><tr><th rowspan="1" colspan="1">Strain</th><th rowspan="1" colspan="1">Genotype<xref ref-type="table-fn" rid="TF6"><sup>a</sup></xref></th><th rowspan="1" colspan="1">Rate (&#215;10<sup>7</sup>)<sup>b</sup></th><th rowspan="1" colspan="1">Ratio<sup>c</sup></th></tr></thead><tbody align="left"><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB163</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>MEC1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">4.0 &#177; 0.6</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.0</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB326</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>sml1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">4.3 &#177; 0.5</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.1</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB312</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>mec1-21</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">5.3 &#177; 1.4</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.3</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB329</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>mec1-21 sml1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">3.8 &#177; 0.1</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.0</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB370</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>dun1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">2.8 &#177; 1.9</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.7</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB369</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>mec1-21 dun1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">1.8 &#177; 0.6</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.5</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">YB380</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">3.2 &#177; 0.5</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.8</td></tr></tbody></table><table-wrap-foot><fn id="TF6"><p textid="49"><sup>a</sup>All strains derived from S288c. For complete genotype (<xref ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>).</p></fn><fn><p textid="50"><sup>b</sup>Rate represents the number of events per cell division; <italic>n</italic> &#8805; 2.</p></fn><fn><p textid="51"><sup>c</sup>Ratio represents rate of SCE in mutant/rate of SCE in wild-type.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
One hypothesis is that higher dNTP levels facilitate DNA replication at stalled replication forks, preventing replication fork regression or the formation of double-strand breaks. Higher dNTP levels can also lead to higher rates of 4NQO-associated mutagenesis (12). We therefore measured rates of spontaneous mutation at CAN1 in wild-type, mec1-21, sml1, mec1-21 sml1, mec1-21 dun1, dun1 and mec1-21 dun1 sml1 strains (Table 4). The rate of spontaneous mutation in wild-type (YB163) was 4 x 10-7, in agreement with Datta et al. (11). In comparison to wild-type, the mutation rate is the same in sml1 and mec1-21 sml1 but lower in mec1-21 dun1 (P < 0.05). The rates of spontaneous mutation are increased approximately2-fold in mec1-21 dun1 sml1 (P < 0.05), in comparison mec1-21 dun1. Thus, higher dNTP levels correlate with the higher rate of spontaneous mutagenesis in mec1-21 dun1 sml1 but not in sml1 strains. Table 4.Rates of spontaneous canavanine resistance in mec1 mutantsStrainGenotypeaRate (x107)bRatiocYB163MEC14.0 +/- 0.61.0YB326sml14.3 +/- 0.51.1YB312mec1-215.3 +/- 1.41.3YB329mec1-21 sml13.8 +/- 0.11.0YB370dun12.8 +/- 1.90.7YB369mec1-21 dun11.8 +/- 0.60.5YB380mec1-21 dun1 sml13.2 +/- 0.50.8aAll strains derived from S288c. For complete genotype (Table 1).bRate represents the number of events per cell division; n >/= 2.cRatio represents rate of SCE in mutant/rate of SCE in wild-type.
###end p 47

###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</sup>
cRatio represents rate of SCE in mutant/rate of SCE in wild-type.
###end p 51
###begin title 52
DISCUSSION
###end title 52
###begin p 53
###xml 28 32 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 231 235 231 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 265 272 265 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 302 307 302 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad52</italic>
###xml 317 319 317 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 390 394 390 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 445 449 445 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 465 469 465 469 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 554 566 554 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 605 609 605 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 614 618 614 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 671 678 671 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 683 687 683 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 763 770 763 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 855 862 855 862 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 867 879 867 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 935 939 935 939 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 981 988 981 988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 1109 1118 1109 1118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1 dun1</italic>
###xml 1222 1226 1222 1226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 1243 1247 1243 1247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 1307 1314 1307 1314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 1319 1323 1319 1323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 1356 1360 1356 1360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 14 19 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The ATR (ATM) yeast homolog MEC1 has a pivotal role in stabilizing stalled DNA replication forks and is required to maintain vital levels of deoxyribonucleotides to ensure that the genome is faithfully replicated. The viability of mec1 hypomorphic mutants, such as mec1-21, is significantly reduced in rad52 mutants (17), suggesting that double-strand breaks are spontaneously generated in mec1 mutants. In this study, we observed that deleting SML1 suppressed the mec1 hyper-recombination phenotypes while increasing the rate of spontaneous mutation in mec1-21 dun1. We compared measurements of dNTPs in SML1 and sml1 deletion strains that contained combinations of the mec1-21 and dun1 mutations, and derived the following conclusions: (i) lower dNTP levels in mec1-21 correlate with an increase in recombination rates, while higher dNTP levels in both mec1-21 and mec1-21 dun1 correlate with a decrease in recombination rates, (ii) DUN1 can suppress homologous recombination in mec1-21 independent of its function in maintaining dNTP levels and (iii) higher dNTP levels increase spontaneous mutagenesis in mec1 dun1 strains. We suggest that increasing dNTP levels reduces the formation of recombinogenic DNA lesions in mec1 hypomorphic and dun1 mutants. This is the first study to measure dNTP levels in mec1-21 and dun1 mutants and to demonstrate that DUN1 is required for maintaining basal dNTP levels.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 135 145 135 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 168 172 164 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 185 192 181 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 194 196 190 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 197 199 193 195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 211 221 207 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 290 297 282 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 404 406 396 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 407 409 399 401 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 410 412 402 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 477 487 469 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 501 508 489 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 685 695 673 679 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 708 715 692 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
These observations may seem to contradict published reports that frequencies of gross chromosomal rearrangements (GCRs) are highest in mec1-Delta, which is deleted for SML1 compared to mec1-21 (31,32). However, mec1-Delta is deficient in both S-phase and G2 checkpoint functions, while the mec1-21 hypomorph retains partial G2 checkpoint function and is less X-ray sensitive compared to the null mutant (17,18,33). We speculate that replication fork collapse is more severe in mec1-Delta, compared to mec1-21. Thus, the combination of replication fork collapse and the deficiency in recombinational repair of double-strand breaks in G2 likely results in the higher rate of GCRs in the mec1-Delta compared to mec1-21.
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Lower dNTP levels contribute to the higher rates of spontaneous recombination
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 5 9 5 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 14 18 14 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 86 93 86 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 252 256 252 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 346 347 346 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 404 406 404 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 429 433 429 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 510 514 510 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 524 528 524 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 624 626 624 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 718 720 718 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 735 739 735 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 857 861 857 861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
Both mec1 and dun1 mutants exhibit lower dNTP levels, compared to wild-type, but only mec1-21 exhibits higher SCE recombination rates. We suggest that the higher recombination rates result from replication forks stalling due to inadequate dNTP levels. MEC1 functions to prevent replication fork collapse, especially at slow zones of replication (3), and when ribonucleotide reductase is inhibited by HU (34). We suggest that the MEC1 function in preventing replication fork collapse reduces spontaneous SCE in dun1 mutants. dun1 mutants do exhibit higher rates of spontaneous heteroallelic gene conversion between homologs (10), and it is possible that sister chromatid gene conversions are not detected in our assay (35). However, in mec1 hypomorphs, stalled replication forks would lead to more replication fork collapse and recombinogenic lesions. Thus, MEC1 has two functions in suppressing recombinogenic lesions: (i) maintaining dNTP levels and (ii) preventing replication fork collapse.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 5 9 5 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 31 38 31 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 42 54 42 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 203 215 203 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 407 419 407 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 sml1</italic>
###xml 587 594 587 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
When SML1 is deleted in either mec1-21 or mec1-21 dun1 strains, we speculate that higher dNTP levels reduce replication fork stalling and thus fewer replication forks collapse. However, we observed that mec1-21 sml1 mutants still exhibited some hyper-recombination between homologs or non-homologous chromosomes when dNTP levels were high. It is likely that we can detect higher levels of translocations in mec1-21 sml1 mutants because there is a lower rate of spontaneous translocations, compared to heteroallelic and SCE, in wild-type. Thus, more recombinogenic lesions still occur in mec1-21, compared to wild-type, even at high dNTP levels.
###end p 57
###begin title 58
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 56 63 56 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
DUN1 suppresses spontaneous homologous recombination in mec1-21
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 24 31 24 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 33 37 33 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 42 54 42 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 364 376 364 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 390 394 390 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 453 459 453 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 461 463 461 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 479 483 479 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CHK1</italic>
###xml 526 530 526 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 534 543 534 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1 sml1</italic>
###xml 575 579 575 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 670 674 670 674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 747 759 747 759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 777 781 777 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 786 790 786 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
Although dNTP levels in mec1-21, dun1 and mec1-21 dun1 are similar, the rates of spontaneous recombination are synergistically increased in the double mutant, compared to the single mutants. We suggest that there may be two different reasons for these observations. First, although the overall dNTP levels are the same, the rate of dNTP production may be lower in mec1-21 dun1, compared to dun1, leading to more replication stalling. Second, Schollaert et al. (36) reported that CHK1 is required for hydroxyurea resistance in dun1 or dun1 sml1 mutants, suggesting additional DUN1 functions in promoting replication. This possibility is supported by the observation that SML1 deletion only partially suppresses the hyper-recombination phenotype in mec1-21 dun1. We suggest that MEC1 and DUN1 may have redundant roles in suppressing recombinogenic breaks.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 6 10 6 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 152 156 152 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DUN1</italic>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3</italic>
###xml 243 245 243 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 313 317 313 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dun1</italic>
###xml 322 334 322 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 406 418 406 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
While MEC1 may prevent replication fork collapse, a possible function of DUN1 in preventing recombinogenic lesions is to promote translesion synthesis. DUN1 functions in promoting spontaneous mutagenesis in both wild-type and in pol3 mutants (11). We observed that the rate of spontaneous mutation was similar in dun1 and mec1-21 dun1. Thus, it is possible that failure to promote translesion synthesis in mec1-21 dun1 leads to more DNA replication stalling at sites of spontaneous damage, increasing the number of collapsed replication forks and recombinogenic lesions.
###end p 60
###begin title 61
###xml 77 89 77 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1</italic>
###xml 122 126 122 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
Spontaneous mutagenesis increases and spontaneous recombination decreases in mec1-21 dun1 as dNTPs levels increase due to SML1 deletion
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 129 131 129 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 337 341 337 341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 475 479 475 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 489 490 489 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 756 773 756 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21 dun1 sml1</italic>
4-NQO-associated mutagenesis increases with higher dNTP levels in strains deleted for genes that encode error-prone polymerases (12), suggesting that replicative polymerases function as translesion polymerases on non-bulky lesions when dNTP levels are higher (12). However, we did not observe higher levels of spontaneous mutagenesis in sml1, compared to wild-type. Considering that Sml1 is degraded in S-phase, the S-phase dNTP levels are likely similar in wild-type and in sml1 mutants (8). We speculate that higher dNTP levels may promote translesion synthesis in cells where replication forks frequently stall, as in S-phase checkpoint mutants when the DNA polymerase encounters slow zones of replication. Here, we speculate that higher dNTP levels in mec1-21 dun1 sml1 promote more translesion synthesis and thus reduce recombinogenic lesions.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
CONCLUSIONS
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1-21</italic>
###xml 95 99 95 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
mec1-21 hyper-recombination phenotype correlates with low dNTP levels and can be suppressed by SML1 mutations. We suggest that higher levels of dNTPs reduce recombinogenic lesions by promoting either replication fork progression or translesion synthesis. This is the first study to show that higher rates of recombination in a mutant deficient in wild-type dNTP levels can be suppressed by increasing dNTP concentrations.
###end p 64
